### Post by markp1989 on 2008-11-30
Rules:
1. Forum guidelines on content apply. In other words, safe for kids and safe for work.
2. Try not to quote embedded images; take a moment to snip them out.
3. Off-topic posts will be edited or moved.
4. Thumbnail your image, or use the forum's attachment system. Full-size embedded images are annoying and will be snipped mercilessly.
5. Take a moment and tell everyone the details of your desktop, such as the theme name, the wallpaper name, the icons and any programs you're using in the image.

Enjoy!

### Post by |{urse on 2008-12-01
^^ almost 2009. Heres a "Kill Fett" wall i made last night. Don't laugh it's my first homemade wallpaper (lol, greyscale not very creative but all from scratch nonetheless). Using modified overglossed gtk2 and black and white icons.

That background for conky is part of the wallpaper so heres my conkyrc for reference.

```
alignment top_right
maximum_width 200
background no
border_width 0
cpu_avg_samples 1
default_color black
default_outline_color grey
default_shade_color dark grey
draw_borders yes
draw_graph_borders yes
draw_outline no
draw_shades no
use_xft yes
xftfont HandelGotD:size=9
xftalpha 0.5
gap_x 4
gap_y 0
minimum_size 5 5
net_avg_samples 2
no_buffers yes
out_to_console no
own_window yes
own_window_class Conky
own_window_type override
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
stippled_borders 0
update_interval 1
uppercase no
use_spacer left
alignment top_right
double_buffer yes

TEXT


${font :size=16}${color}${alignc}${time %I:%M:%S %p}$color $font
${font :size=12}${color}${alignc}${time %A, %B %e, %G}$color$font

SYSTEM ${color  FFC033}$hr${color white}
OS:${alignr}${color white}Ubuntu 8.04
Uptime:${alignr}${color white}$uptime_short
Processes:${alignr}${color white}${running_processes} of ${processes}
AC Power:${alignr}${acpiacadapter}
Battery:${alignr}${battery_percent}%


${color black}CPU ${color FFC033}${hr}${color white}
Frequency:${alignr}${color white}$freq MHz
CPU Usage:${alignr}${color white}${cpu}% ${cpubar cpu0 5,50}
CPU Temp:${alignr}${color white}${acpitempf}°F

${color black}MEMORY ${color FFC033}$hr
${color white}RAM:
${alignc}Using $mem of $memmax
${membar 5}
Buffered:${alignr}${buffers}
Cached:${alignr}${cached}

SWAP:
${alignc}Using ${fs_used /dev/sda5} of ${fs_size /dev/sda5}
${fs_bar 5 /dev/sda5}

${color black}DISKS ${color FFC033}$hr${color}
${color white}/:$alignr ${color white}${fs_used /} of ${fs_size /}
${fs_bar 5 /}
${color white}/home:$alignr ${color white}${fs_used /home} of ${fs_size /home}
${fs_bar 5 /home}
${color}    Read:${color}${diskio_read} ${alignr}${color}Write:${color}${diskio_write}
${diskiograph_read 15,95 000000 ffffff} ${alignr}${diskiograph_write 15,95 000000 ffffff} 
${color}
${color black}NETWORK ${color  FFC033}$hr${color}
${color white}${alignc}Local IP: ${addr ath0}
${color white}${alignc}Public IP: ${execi 3600 wget -O - http://whatismyip.org/ | tail}
${color black}Down: ${color}${downspeed ath0}Kb/s${color  grey}${alignr}${color}Up: ${color}${upspeed ath0}Kb/s${color}
${upspeedgraph ath0 15,95 000000 ffffff} ${alignr}${downspeedgraph ath0 15,95 000000 ffffff}

${color}Inbound: ${tcp_portmon 1 32767 count} ${alignr}${color}Outbound: ${tcp_portmon 32768 61000 count}
Total: ${totaldown eth0} ${alignr}Total: ${totalup ath0}
${color white}$hr
```

heres a link to the wallpaper
[http://i283.photobucket.com/albums/kk302/SuperiorYeti/fetttargetinvert.png]("http://i283.photobucket.com/albums/kk302/SuperiorYeti/fetttargetinvert.png")

### Post by Twilight in Zero on 2008-12-01
etnlIcarus, perhaps you should try porting to Metacity, and using GTK Window Decorator. Emerald is becoming deprecated anyways.

Two shots from me, light and dark. I'm using the dark version for now. I was hoping I could just use the same GTK (and metacity) for light and dark themes, but there's not enough contrast. D:

DE: GNOME
GTK: My own, called Twilight Murrina. Not published anywhere yet.
Metacity: Same as above.
Icons: GNOME
Font: Vera Sans 9, subpixel, slight autohint.

I'd try out some other fonts, and lose the hinting, but it irks me when I see mnemonic underlines that aren't horizontally aligned. Wish I could do something about that. D:

### Post by Piraja on 2008-12-02
Hey,

does anyone know if its possible to make and use different Conky configurations for different desktop environments and window managers, and if, then how — I mean I'm using both Gnome and Fluxbox, and as you can see, what works for one does not necessarily work for the other.

Fluxbox: [[IMG]http://www.aijaa.com/img/t/00207/3178769.t.png[/IMG]](http://www.aijaa.com/v.php?i=3178769.png) Gnome: [[IMG]http://www.aijaa.com/img/t/00280/3178775.t.png[/IMG]](http://www.aijaa.com/v.php?i=3178775.png)

PFA my Fluxbox and Conky configuration files. **P.S.( addition/edition)** You see that if I fix it in Gnome...

[[IMG]http://www.aijaa.com/img/t/00065/3179056.t.png[/IMG]](http://www.aijaa.com/v.php?i=3179056.png) ... it's... [[IMG]http://www.aijaa.com/img/t/00713/3179072.t.png[/IMG]](http://www.aijaa.com/v.php?i=3179072.png)

... no longer nice in Fluxbox, and vice versa. NB: in the Tarball, the Conky config file is conky.conf, but I made a .conkyrc for my home folder just a few moments ago. As always, feel free to use and modify the config files!

**P.S.** I decided to make a [new thread]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6293023") on this.

**P.P.S.** What a stupdid question. Its obvious answer:
```
conky --help
```
and then:
```
conky -c ~./<my-optional-conky-config-file>
```

**P.P.P.S.** Yet, maybe I could specify the Fluxbox-specific conf-file in Fluxbox's startup file, too...

**P.P.P.P.S.** [Yes, it worked]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6293672&postcount=2")!

**P.P.P.P.P.S.** PFA my .fluxbox directory. Modify it as you like!
I never use emoticons, but here's an exception that proves the rule:

):P

### Post by supersonicdarky on 2008-12-03
> **el mariachi said:**
> could you share you conky?
like the setup a lot :D

wished I had a *real* dell monitor :(

```
background yes
double_buffer yes
use_xft yes

default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white
own_window_transparent yes

own_window yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 

draw_borders no
border_margin 0
draw_shades no

gap_x 5
gap_y 59

alignment bottom_right

update_interval 0.5

default_color  ffffff

use_xft no
xftfont silkscreen:pixelsize=8

use_spacer no
minimum_size 200 10

TEXT
${alignr}${time %A}, ${color c4cbff}${time %b %d %Y}${color} 
${alignr}Up: ${color c4cbff}${uptime_short}${color} 
${alignr}Cpu: ${color c4cbff}${cpu}% ${color}${cpugraph 8,30} 
${alignr}${color }Mem: ${color c4cbff}$memperc% ${color}
${alignr}/: ${color c4cbff}${fs_used_perc /}%${color} | /data: ${color c4cbff}${fs_used_perc /media/data}%${color} | /ext: ${color c4cbff}${fs_used_perc /media/ext}%${color} 
${alignr}Down: ${color c4cbff}${downspeed wlan0} ${color}k/s ${downspeedgraph wlan0 8,30} 
${alignr}Up: ${color c4cbff}${upspeed wlan0}${color} k/s ${upspeedgraph wlan0 8,30} 
${alignr}Currently ${color c4cbff}${execi 600 python ~/scripts/weather.py CAXX0343 c t} ${color}C, ${color c4cbff}${execi 600 python ~/scripts/weather.py CAXX0343 c c} 
```

```
background yes
double_buffer yes
use_xft yes

default_shade_color black
default_outline_color white
own_window_transparent yes

own_window yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 

draw_borders no
border_margin 0

draw_shades no

gap_x 10
gap_y 935
alignment top_left

update_interval 0.5

default_color  ffffff

use_xft no
xftfont silkscreen:pixelsize=8
minimum_size 300 50

mpd_host 192.168.1.111

TEXT
${if_running mpd}$mpd_smart
$mpd_status $mpd_elapsed/$mpd_length
${mpd_bar 4,100}
$endif
```

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2008-12-03
> **h!v said:**
> Yes, that's what I all meant. 
There should be somewhere that css ( or code for this) ( add-on folder?). I'd be gratefull for file or at least name that style. Looks way better than this crapy red or black/white skin.

Cheers

You should have a folder ~/.opera/styles/user/ where you can drop custom css files. To apply them to the site, you have to right click on the site and select 'Edit Site Preferences', click the Display tab and select your custom style sheet and then in the menubar click View-->Style and select user mode. It's complicated, I know, but loading greasemonkey scripts is relatively easy. Go to Tools-->Preferences-->Advanced-->Content and click the "Javascript Options" button. At the bottom there is a box, "User JS Files". You have to enter a directory. I make a directory ~/.opera/userjs/ and use that. Then on userstyles.org when you see the "Load as userjs" button, you can click that and save the file in ~/.opera/userjs/ and the next time you go to the site, it will be applied.

---

> **eightmillion said:**
> You should have a folder ~/.opera/styles/user/ where you can drop custom css files. To apply them to the site, you have to right click on the site and select 'Edit Site Preferences', click the Display tab and select your custom style sheet and then in the menubar click View-->Style and select user mode. It's complicated, I know, but loading greasemonkey scripts is relatively easy. Go to Tools-->Preferences-->Advanced-->Content and click the "Javascript Options" button. At the bottom there is a box, "User JS Files". You have to enter a directory. I make a directory ~/.opera/userjs/ and use that. Then on userstyles.org when you see the "Load as userjs" button, you can click that and save the file in ~/.opera/userjs/ and the next time you go to the site, it will be applied.

I was asking mrgnash for name of theme/css/code file, not for tutorial. I know how it works already ;). Question marks are there cuz I'm not sure about where FF holds its add-on files ( I'm not fan of Gecko at all).
But thank you for effort of explaining tho.

Cheers

---

### Post by h!v on 2008-12-04
> **eightmillion said:**
> You should have a folder ~/.opera/styles/user/ where you can drop custom css files. To apply them to the site, you have to right click on the site and select 'Edit Site Preferences', click the Display tab and select your custom style sheet and then in the menubar click View-->Style and select user mode. It's complicated, I know, but loading greasemonkey scripts is relatively easy. Go to Tools-->Preferences-->Advanced-->Content and click the "Javascript Options" button. At the bottom there is a box, "User JS Files". You have to enter a directory. I make a directory ~/.opera/userjs/ and use that. Then on userstyles.org when you see the "Load as userjs" button, you can click that and save the file in ~/.opera/userjs/ and the next time you go to the site, it will be applied.

If it's not working ( actualy that style didn't work from start),[ go with this tutorial( for anyone intrested)]("http://www.lastfm.pl/group/Last.fm+CSS+Color+Changer/forum/30401/_/253097")
Style needs some workin on it too, tho. Bah work for later on :popcorn:.

For now SS from XP-box

### Post by h!v on 2008-12-04
> **Giant Speck said:**
> I wish they had styles like that for Pandora Radio.  :(

In Opera this style will work for any site, if you follow that link( edit script and save as CSS file). 
In FireFox just edit this section
```

@-moz-document url

``` for other links in style file( you can do that via plugin options).

Could not work full but after some polishing moves can be easy done.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-12-04
Okay, so I decided to try out KDE 4.2 Beta 1 on Kubuntu.

So far, everything is working fine EXCEPT plasmoids on the desktop.  Every time I try to add a widget to the desktop it freezes Plasma and I have to restart it.

For some reason, when I upgraded to KDE 4.2, it tried to install kde4libs-bin, but failed because it said that kde4libs-bin needed kdelibs5 (4:4.1.2-0ubuntu1~hardy1~ppa2), whereas kdelibs5 (4:4.1.80-0ubuntu1~intrepid1~ppa2) is installed.  The main problem with that is, is that a there are a few programs from the upgrade that rely on the newer version of kdelibs5 and would be uninstalled if I was to force-version kdelibs5.

Bottom line: It looks pretty, but doesn't work completely correctly.

Screenshot time:

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2008-12-06
> **~LoKe said:**
> Is that AwesomeWM?  If so, can I get all the info? (configs, Xdefaults, etc)

Yes, it's awesome.  It's a version of awesome-git that I compiled back in October, but I think the config should still work with current versions.  You'll also need wicked-git installed.

I think I maybe got the config from gigamo (my theme is called gigamo-light) but I really don't remember to be perfectly honest.

Anyway, here's my .config/awesome and my .Xdefaults.  If you need anything else feel free to ask.  Also, the rc.lua has a few paths hardcoded in that you may need to change (I'm sure you know, I used your guide for awesome at one time).  Also, I think awesome might crash if you don't have the artwiz fonts installed (or you can just change the font in the config)

### Post by RiceMonster on 2008-12-08
> **ddnev45 said:**
> I admire your persistence. I got Arch installed and booted to a functioning command line, but the package manager refused to work; had internet access (could ping other sites) and could access the chosen mirror from the other computer. Scoured the Arch sites for about an hour then went back to Debian.

Arch, was the first Linux distro I ever used. I had X and the package manager working almost immediately after install. I had no idea what I was doing though, and in the end my system was a mess, so I used Ubuntu for a few months to learn how to do things, then I went distro hopping and ended up back on Arch. Got it working the first try when I went back :).

Anyway, your package manager may not have been working because you probably didn't select a mirror properly on install. If you didn't you have to go into /etc/pacman.d/ and there will be a file for each repo, containing a list of all the mirrors. Uncomment a mirror for each one, then run pacman -Syu and it will create /etc/pacman.d/mirrorlist.

Yeah, that happened to me before.

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2008-12-08
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Still haven't figured out what my timezone is supposed to be, or how to setup user accounts (currently running as root).

[http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Official_Arch_Linux_Install_Guide#User_Management](http://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Official_Arch_Linux_Install_Guide#User_Management)

for timezone, no doubt you've heard about /etc/rc.conf a million times if you've looked at arch's documentation. in that file, there is an entry called "TIMEZONE". just put your timezone in there and you should be good to go. if you need suggestions for timezones, /etc/rc.conf suggests you look in /usr/share/zoneinfo.

---

```
adduser
```

and follow to instructions the only thing you might need to look up are the groups you need to add your user to.

### Post by Piraja on 2008-12-08
> **komodojay said:**
> I love your conky any way you can link to the file your using?

Thanks for the interest, here you go:

```
# .clock_conkyrc
# Conky sample configuration
# [previously] modified by Peter R Tynan [and re-modified by Piraja]
# clock layout based upon cardinals_fan conkyrc http://crayon.pastebin.org/27880
#
# the list of variables has been removed from this file in favour
# of keeping the documentation more maintainable.
# Check http://conky.sf.net for an up-to-date-list.
# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background yes

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Font if xft not used
# font -monotype-courier new-demibold-r-normal-17-120-100-100-*-0-microsoft-cp1251

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont HandleGotD:size=7

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 0.8

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 5.0

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window yes

# If own_window is yes, you may use type normal, desktop or override
own_window_type override

# Use pseudo transparency with own_window?
own_window_transparent yes

# If own_window is yes, these window manager hints may be used
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 200 600

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no

# Draw borders around graphs
draw_graph_borders yes

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 8

# border margins
border_margin 4

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color 703621
default_shade_color 085063
default_outline_color 085063

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right
#alignment none

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 10
gap_y 20

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about? This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer yes

# variable is given either in format $variable or in ${variable}. Latter
# allows characters right after the variable and must be used in network
# stuff because of an argument

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen
TEXT
${offset -5}${voffset 5}${color 085063}${font Droid Sans Mono:size=72}${time %H}
${offset 129}${voffset -155}${font Droid Sans Mono:size=30}${time %M}
${offset 131}${voffset -25}${color}${font font Droid Sans Mono::size=14}${time %b}
${offset 132}${voffset -5}${time %d}
${voffset 5}${color black}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=14}SYSTEM:
${color black}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9}UPTIME:$color $uptime ${color black}- Load:$color $loadavg
${voffset 5}${color black}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size9}CPU USAGE:$color ${cpu}% ${cpubar}
${color black}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9}RAM USAGE:$color $mem/$memmax 
$memperc% $membar
${voffset 5}${color black}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9}SWAP USAGE:$color $swap/$swapmax 
$swapperc% ${swapbar}
${voffset 5}${color black}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9}Processes:$color $processes ${color black}Running:$color $running_processes
${voffset 5}${color black}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9}Name PID CPU% MEM%
${voffset 5}${color}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9} ${top name 1} ${top pid 1} ${top cpu 1} ${top mem 1}
${voffset 5}${color}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9} ${top name 2} ${top pid 2} ${top cpu 2} ${top mem 2}
${voffset 5}${color}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9} ${top name 3} ${top pid 3} ${top cpu 3} ${top mem 3}
${voffset 5}${color black}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=14}FILE SYSTEM:
${color}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9} / $color${fs_free_perc /}% ${fs_size /} ${fs_bar /}
${voffset 5} /home $color${fs_free_perc /home}% ${fs_size /home} ${fs_bar /home}
${voffset 5}${color black}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=14}NETWORK:
${color}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9}DOWN: ${downspeed wlan0} k/s ${offset 75}UP: ${upspeed wlan0} k/s
${voffset 10}${if_running mpd}${color black}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=14}MPD:
${color}${font HeldustryFTVBasic Demi:size=9}$mpd_smart
$mpd_album
$mpd_status $mpd_elapsed/$mpd_length
$endif
```

I don't remember where I originally copied the file from, but as you can see on line 3, at least Peter R. Tynan has been involved in creating it. Since then, I have customised it quite a bit.

[COLOR="Red"]Hey, I definitely should have highlighted also the fact on line 4: "clock layout based upon cardinals_fan conkyrc http://crayon.pastebin.org/27880"! Thanks to cardinals_fan![/COLOR]

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-12-08
I may have fixed my font rendering problem.

I increased the DPI from 96 to 120 and then reduced the text size to 7.

For some reason at 96 DPI, rendering options weren't working.

Again, ignore the dock buttons.  The blurriness of that text has nothing to do with my rendering settings.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2008-12-09
> **Opeth115 said:**
> I've been reading about lunar Linux and what are the advantages of it?  I see you compile everything from source is this correct?  If so isn't that bassically gentoo?

yes, both lunar and gentoo r source based distros. but i find lunar a tad bit faster than gentoo. now its just a personal opinion. i used to love gentoo sometime back. but then ran into a string of problems with portage :( and it was a never ending story. this was primarily the reason y i wanted to try Lunar rather than gentoo again. and i really love the lunar package management system. building a module is so well thought out, and i can build it according to my needs, so i can get rid of the unnecessary crap. but another aspect is that i can also create my new modules pretty easily in lunar, by moving the changed modules into a new folder, and thats it. i find it doin this way much easier than using overlays in gentoo.

setting up the bootstrap system was also pretty easy. and the best part is also the fact that moonbase (lunar's repository database) have only one version of each module or package, eliminating the necessity of masking/unmasking. theres always svn where i can fetch my older builds if needed. 

overall there's not much of a difference between gentoo and lunar, but gentoo simply didn't work for me. so i guess its a case of personal preference. btw does gentoo still do etc files merging? never really liked it!

---

### Post by dariusdwtt on 2008-12-09
Piraja:

I liked your lined paper terminal idea so much, that I made one of my own :)

I've lined up the lines so that the words in the terminal always sit just perfectly on them,
and put in a margin that is lined up with the prompt, so your prompt will always be easy to find and the writing will be easier to read!

I'm gonna put it in the ubuntu-artwork wiki and see if they can implement it.

Considering that most new users are not used to the terminal it could help them!

:guitar:

### Post by Piraja on 2008-12-11
**P.S. to my post # 366 and a hopefully useful hint for MPD and Lyricsdownloader users:**

It seems actually a good idea to remove the MPD stuff from the "main" conky and put it at the beginning of another Conky that uses the Lyricsdownloader script (courtesy of Eightmillion). Now when I'm listening to instrumental music or a track whose lyrics cannot be downloaded from Leo's Lyrics or Lyrics Wiki or whatever, the "music conky" still shows the artist, track and album info. Which is nice.

Still, I wonder why I'm now getting that 98% RAM usage...?

The photo in the background is titled "Smoke Wallpaper #4" and it's by [.robbie]("http://www.flickr.com/photos/rtv/2395920004/"), found via a Creative Commons search.

It's cool that you are a (yuck) windows lover but don't knock KDE/linux bar to windows on a untrue fact. It may be possible in windows with so called hacks and stuff but the beauty of linux is the default option of instant customization and endless possibilities and looks and to me any linux(KDE/Gnome) bar is more intuitive and useful.Not to get involved in this little debate but genuinely curious: can you select multiple windows from a tasklist and tile/cascade just the selected ones?

I'm pretty sure kicker couldn't even do that, despite it being introduced into XP back in 02 (though Windows blows in pretty much every other window management department). Last time I used plasma panel, KDE4.1 was too unstable to use for a prolonged amount of time so I never thought to check.

### Post by cookieofdoom on 2008-12-12
> **What is in a name? said:**
> Just some more changes to my KDE 4.2 desktop... Nothing major:

[[IMG]http://e.imagehost.org/t/0178/ecra.jpg[/IMG]](http://e.imagehost.org/view/0178/ecra) [[IMG]http://e.imagehost.org/t/0269/ecra2.jpg[/IMG]](http://e.imagehost.org/view/0269/ecra2)

If you mean you can't change fonts for Amarok specifically, it would appear that way (although I don't know much about how KDE does things). You can alter your system wide fonts and it should affect Amarok2. I just switched all my fonts to oblique, restarted Amarok, and it seemed to work.

How stable is KDE4.2 for you? It's kinda buggy for me. Plasma really likes to crash, and the menu is really slow. I'd upload a screenshot of my setup, but it's really not very pretty right now.

---

### Post by What is in a name? on 2008-12-12
I'll have to note that I'm using **Project Neon**'s repository. Mileage may vary if you use other repositories, or even other distros, I guess, but I decided to share this issue just in case. So thanks for the replies:

> **raul_ said:**
> Doesn't Amarok use your system fonts? It's working here

Well, no it doesn't, as you can see in the screenshots. My system fonts are Legacy Sans, but Amarok still appears with the default Sans and Sans Serif fonts (which don't bother me as much because Sans Serif looks a lot like the Most Holy of the fonts, Helvetica, but still...). Perhaps there's some workaround I'll have to look up in the Web.

> **cookieofdoom said:**
> If you mean you can't change fonts for Amarok specifically, it would appear that way (although I don't know much about how KDE does things). You can alter your system wide fonts and it should affect Amarok2. I just switched all my fonts to oblique, restarted Amarok, and it seemed to work.

How stable is KDE4.2 for you? It's kinda buggy for me. Plasma really likes to crash, and the menu is really slow. I'd upload a screenshot of my setup, but it's really not very pretty right now.

After doing all the tweaking I want, KDE 4.2 is pretty stable indeed. I have experienced some crashes when moving Plasma applets from the panel to the desktop, or when resizing certain applets, or even when I resized the panel too quickly (perhaps my video card is also playing some influence here). But other than that, KDE 4.2 beta is (surprisingly) fast, feels solid... I think I'll stick with it for some time now.

---

### Post by billgoldberg on 2008-12-12
I just added a little conky to my current setup.

The .conkyrc file

> background yes
use_xft no
xftfont Bitstream Vera Sans:size=7
xftalpha 0.8
update_interval 0.5
own_window yesEdit/Delete Message
own_window_type normal
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_border no
draw_graph_borders yes
stippled_borders no
default_color white
default_shade_color black
alignment top_left
minimum_size 1425
maximum_width 1800
gap_y 7
gap_x 20
use_spacer no
no_buffers yes

TEXT
${color Tan1}Kernel ${color DimGray}: $kernel  |  ${color Tan1}Processors ${color DimGray}: CPU1  ${cpu cpu1}% - CPU2 ${cpu cpu2}%  |  ${color Tan1}Memory ${color DimGray}: ${mem} of ${memmax} used  |  ${color Tan1}Processes ${color DimGray}: $running_processes of $processes running  |  ${color Tan1} HDD: ${color DimGray} ${fs_used /} of ${fs_size /} used  |  ${color Tan1}Swap ${color DimGray}: $swap of $swapmax used  |   ${color Tan1}IP on eth0 ${color DimGray}: ${addr eth0}  |  ${color Tan1}Date ${color DimGray}: ${time %B %d}  |  ${color Tan1}Time${color DimGray}: ${time %I:%M}h 


In case you are wondering, the background on the conky file is just painted on the wallpaper, using the gimp.

### Post by ddnev45 on 2008-12-13
> **indecisive said:**
> How did you get (if you did) Fvwm to recognize GTK?

I have the line:

```
gtk-icon-theme-name="Eikon"
```

in ~/.gtkrc-2.0 so that the system tray (trayer) uses the Eikon theme. The menu icons I made myself from various sets and put in ~/.icons/22x22; used an environment variable in .fvwm2rc to set image path and make the menu entries simpler:

```
ImagePath ~/.icons/22x22:
```

I don't use gtk themes in fvwm, I did the colorsets myself.

---

### Post by |{urse on 2008-12-16
minimalist ^^

.conkyrc
```
background yes
use_xft yes
xftfont Oblique:size=7
xftalpha 0.8
update_interval 2
own_window no
double_buffer yes
draw_shades no
draw_outline yes
stippled_borders no
border_margin 0
border_width 1
default_color white
default_shade_color black
alignment top_left
minimum_size 1262
gap_x 9
gap_y 9
use_spacer no
no_buffers yes
uppercase yes

TEXT
${alignc}${color white}Ubuntu $sysname $kernel ${color darkgrey}on ${color white}$nodename ${color darkgrey}[${color white}${freq}Mhz ${execi 1000 cat /proc/cpuinfo | grep 'model name' | sed -e 's/model name.*: //'}${color darkgrey}] |${color white}$uptime_short ${color darkgrey}uptime at ${color white}$cpu% ${color darkgrey}cpu load with ${color white}${mem}b${color darkgrey} of ${color white}${memmax}b${color darkgrey} (${color white}$memperc%${color darkgrey}) used by ${color white}$processes ${color darkgrey}processes
${alignc}${color white}${fs_used /}b${color darkgrey} of ${color white}${fs_size /}b${color darkgrey} root partition used, ${color white}${fs_used /home}b${color darkgrey} of ${color white}${fs_size /home}b${color darkgrey} home partition used | ${color white}${downspeed ath0} kbps${color darkgrey} down (${color white}${totaldown ath0}b${color darkgrey} total), ${color white}${upspeed ra0} kbps${color darkgrey} up (${color white}${totalup ath0}b${color darkgrey} total) on ${color white}${addr ath0}
```

$home/.config/tint/tintrc

```
#---------------------------------------------
# TINT CONFIG FILE
#---------------------------------------------

#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL
#---------------------------------------------
panel_show_all_desktop = 0
panel_monitor = 1
panel_position = bottom center
panel_size = 900 28
panel_margin = 5 2
panel_padding = 8 2
font_shadow = 0


#---------------------------------------------
# PANEL BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
panel_rounded = 7
#panel_border_width = 0
panel_background_color = #333333 70
panel_border_color = #ffffff 18

#---------------------------------------------
# TASKS
#---------------------------------------------
task_text_centered = 0
task_width = 0
task_margin = 2
task_padding = 5
task_icon_size = 0
task_font = Oblique 9
task_font_color = #000000 70
task_active_font_color = #000000 85

#---------------------------------------------
# TASK BACKGROUND AND BORDER
#---------------------------------------------
task_rounded = 5
task_background_color = #C0C0C0 50
task_active_background_color = #C0C0C0 70
task_border_width = 1
task_border_color = #ffffff 18
task_active_border_color = #ffffff 10

#---------------------------------------------
# CLOCK
#---------------------------------------------
time1_format = %H:%M
time1_font = sans 8
time2_format = %A %d %B
time2_font = Oblique 6
clock_font_color = #ffffff 76

#---------------------------------------------
# MOUSE ACTION ON TASK
#---------------------------------------------
mouse_middle = none
mouse_right = close
mouse_scroll_up = toggle
mouse_scroll_down = iconify
```

.stalonetrayrc
```
# background <color> # color can be specified as an HTML hex triplet or
# as a name from rgb.txt, note that '#' must be quoted
background "ffffff 18"

# decorations <decspec> # set trays window decorations; possible values for
# decspec are: all, title, border, none
decorations border

# display <display name> # as usual

# dbg_level <int> # controls the amount of debug info (for this setting to
# have effect, stalonetray sources must have been
# configured and compiled with --enable-debug)
# dbg_level 0

# fuzzy_edges [<level>] # enable fuzzy edges and set fuzziness level. level
# can be from 0 (disabled) to 3; this setting works
# with tinting and/or transparent and/or pixmap
# backgrounds (NEW in 0.7)
fuzzy_edges 3

# geometry <geometry> # tray's geometry in standard X notation
geometry 124x24+0-0

# grow_gravity <gravity> # one of N, S, E, W, NW, NE, SW, SE; tray will grow
# in the direction opposite to one specified by
# grow_gravity; if horizontal or vertical
# direction is not specified, tray will not grow in
# that direction
grow_gravity NW

# icon_gravity <gravity> # icon placement gravity, one of NW, NE, SW, SE
icon_gravity NW

# icon_size <int> # specifies dimensions of typical icon slot
icon_size 18

# ignore_icon_resize [<bool>] # ignore icon attempts to resize their windows
# (NEW in 0.7)
ignore_icon_resize false

# max_width <int> # specifies maximal tray's width (0 = no limit)
max_width 0

# max_height <int> # specifies maximal tray's height (0 = no limit)
max_height 28

# no_shrink [<bool>] # disables shrink-back mode (NEW in 0.7)
no_shrink false

# parent_bg [<bool>] # whether to use pseudo-transparency
# (looks better when reparented into smth like FvwmButtons)
parent_bg false

# pixmap_bg <path_to_xpm> # use pixmap from specified xpm file for (tiled) background
# pixmap_bg /home/user/.stalonetraybg.xpm

# respect_icon_hints [<bool>] # try to respect icon hints (NEW in 0.7)
respect_icon_hints false

# skip_taskbar [<bool>] # hide tray`s window from the taskbar
skip_taskbar true

# sticky [<bool>] # make a tray`s window sticky across the
# desktops/pages
sticky true

# tint_color <color> # set tinting color (NEW in 0.7)
tint_color gray

# tint_level <level> # set tinting level; level ranges from 0 (disabled)
# to 255 (NEW in 0.7)
tint_level 200

# transparent [<bool>] # whether to use root-transparency (background
# image must be set with Esetroot or compatible utility)
transparent true

# vertical [<bool>] # whether to use vertical layout (horisontal layout
# is used by default)
vertical false

# window_layer <layer> # set the EWMH-compatible window layer; one of:
# bootom, normal, top
window_layer bottom

# window_type <type> # set the EWMH-compatible window type; one of:
# dock, normal, toolbar, utility
window_type dock

# withdrawn [<bool>] # start withdrawn (NEW in 0.7, prior to that
# withdrawn mode was default!)
withdrawn false

# xsync [<bool>] # whether to operate on X server synchronously (SLOOOOW)
xsync false
```

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-12-17
I've been working on my Manganite theme, trying to take it in a new direction.

I took a theme called Murrine Redmond, which I found on GNOME-Look, replaced its colors with the Manganite colors.  Then I tweaked some of the widget settings and recolored the menubar, toolbar, and progressbar.

Then, I decided to experiment with the pixbuf engine.

I took the background pixmap from the Mira theme and recolored it to somewhat match the color of Manganite's window background.

So here it is:

GTK: Custom
Font: MgOpen Cosmetica
Dock: Cairo-dock
Conky: Mira Red, custom-modified
Wallpaper: A redder modification of the red wallpaper from the pack "[Colored Backgrounds]("http://alexander-gg.deviantart.com/art/Colored-Backgrounds-102172919")" by Alexander-GG
Swiftfox: Elementary, with a custom tabbar

---

### Post by N00b-un-2 on 2008-12-19
OS: Ubuntu 8.10
WM: gtk/emerald
Dock: avant-window-navigator
Theme: Modified Slickness-Black theme
Icons: Combination of black-white_2-Gloss_big, LiNsta3.0, and a few I made or modded myself, like the Fruity Loops icon seen in the dock,the Audacity icon from the Linsta set with the wave color changed to match the rest of the theme.  The small winged icon next to Fruity Loops is an icon of the Enlisted Air Warfare Specialist badge, or "Wings" for short.  I'm a Petty Officer in the US Navy and that is a qualification I'm working towards right now.
I like the black-white icon set for the most part, but I didn't like the volume slider or the wireless signal icons.  The wifi icon I created myself, and the volume icon is from the "hicolor" icon set I think.

I was using screenlets to monitor my system resources, but I switched to using Conky yesterday, as you can see in the bottom left.  I'm just learning how to set up Conky, but I like it a lot better because of how configurable it is.  It's almost like HTML in it's simplicity.

### Post by elmer_42 on 2008-12-19
[QUOTE=Everybody]Give us the Conky config and the font, and nobody gets hurt.[/QUOTE]
It's actually two config files because as far as I know there is no way to vertically center text in Conky unless you use a seperate config file and do some tricky gap_y work. As you can see in the config file, the font that displays the month is Avant Garde. I had to do some tricky Googling (hint: use filetype:otf) to find it. The part with all the system stuff is this:
```
own_window yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none 
use_xft yes
override_utf8_locale yes
xftfont glisp 
update_interval 1.0
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
stippled_borders 0
border_margin 0
border_width 0
default_color c0c0c0 
own_window_transparent yes
minimum_size 1 1
maximum_width 1440
alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right
gap_x 162 
gap_y 35

TEXT
${color 303030}CPU:${color} ${cpu}% ${color 303030}Mem:${color} $memperc% ${color 303030}Down:${color} ${downspeed eth0}Kb/s ${color 303030}Up:${color} ${upspeed eth0}Kb/s
```
and the config that outputs the date:
```
own_window yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
use_spacer none 
use_xft yes
uppercase yes
override_utf8_locale yes
xftfont ITC Avant Garde Gothic Std:size=40
update_interval 1.0
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
stippled_borders 0
border_margin 0
border_width 0
default_color c0c0c0 
own_window_transparent yes
minimum_size 1 1
maximum_width 200 
#alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right
gap_x 0
gap_y 13 

TEXT
${font ITC Avant Garde Gothic Std:bold:size=40}${time %d}${font}${time %b}
```

---

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2008-12-20
> **crl0901 said:**
> I tried attaching it to the post but it kept telling me that the file was invalid or something.

Most likely the file size was too large.  There is a limit of 976.6KB for most attachment types.  In case of large images, most people upload them to some third party and then either just include a link or use the correct bbcode to include a thumbnail image (which links to the larger one).

### Post by jordanmthomas on 2008-12-21
> **urukrama said:**
> Could you post your ~/.screenrc? Thank you.

Sure thing, it's not really mine, I got it from stxza's awesome config.
```
#-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
# ~/.screenrc
# Last modified 18/11/2008
#-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

startup_message off
vbell off
vbell_msg "[[[ ding ]]]"
activity "active: %n (%t) [%w:%s]"
bell "bell: %n (%t) [%w:%s]^G"
msgwait 2 # 1 second messages
defscrollback 10000

autodetach on
deflogin on
nethack on
defutf8 on
altscreen on
defbce on
nonblock on
defhstatus "screen: ^En (^Et)"
term screen-256color
terminfo rxvt* 'Co#256:AB=\E[48;5;%dm:AF=\E[38;5;%dm'
#termcapinfo rxvt|rxvt-unicode|urxvt|rxvt-256color|screen|xs|rxvt ti@:te@
#sorendition +b kG

#[randy@voodoo] updates :: none                        1 irssi  [2 vim .screenrc]
#hardstatus alwayslastline "%{= dd} %=%-w[%n %t]%+w" 
caption always "%{= dd}%{b}[ %=%{w}%?%-Lw%?%{b}(%{W}%n*%f %t%?(%u)%?%{b})%{w}%?%+Lw%?%?%= %{b}][%{B} %H %{W}%l %{b}]"

# Default apps
# screen -t irc weechat-curses
screen zsh
screen htop

bindkey "^[Od" prev
bindkey "^[Oc" next

```

### Post by darsu on 2008-12-21
Cinan's is lovely. The word "understated" fits too few desktops in these threads.

Alas, my current theme is busier than anything I've had in years. I tinkered it around a Pompeii fresco on the cover of a [favorite novel](http://www.amazon.com/Death-Virgil-Hermann-Broch/dp/0679755489). I made a background to incorporate it with GIMP (colorized plasma, filled rectangles, then mosaic distortion); the Openbox theme is "Flux", QT has "KDE Classic" style, all with colors adjusted to fit, and there's two Conkies with matching colors. Title font is Post Mediaeval, KDE font is Gentium.

The JPG is a bit smudgy...

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-12-23
> **Prefix100 said:**
> That is the nicest desktop I've seen yet.
Aww shucks. Thankyou.
> **billgoldberg said:**
> Yes, I've installed AVG.
I've heard so many horror stories about AVG recently. Personally, I suggest you switch to Avira Anti-vir.
> **kallum said:**
> Can anyone tell me how to get my desktop like this ? I've only just downloaded Ubuntu and don't know what all these codes are everyone is posting.

It's called *conky*.

Do a:

$ sudo apt-get install conky

Or you can open up Synaptic Package Manager and search for conky if you're more comfortable using a graphic interface.

And check out [this thread](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=281865) for a guide on how to configure it, as well as the [official documentation](http://conky.sourceforge.net/documentation.html).

And if you were referring to the OSX-style dock, that's called *AWN* or *Avant Window Navigator*, which is in the repos as well and can be installed via synaptic or apt-get.

### Post by eightmillion on 2008-12-24
> **armageddon08 said:**
> Details please.......ur desktop sure looks sexy..:)

Thanks. It's KDE 4.2 beta. Here's the details:

Window decorations:  [Dworkin Dark]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/Dworkin+Dark?content=95350")
The version that I'm using in the screenshot is slightly darker. I also have a version for emerald.

Widget style: Bespin
This is in the repositories. You'll have to build it yourself if you want to use it with 4.2

Wallpaper: [Something I found somewhere.]("http://e.imagehost.org/view/0835/brain")

Clock: [3D Desktop Clock]("http://kde-look.org/content/show.php/3D+Desktop+Clock?content=95681")

Dock: Cairo dock
The icons are custom, but they're based on [these.]("http://leechiahan.deviantart.com/art/Lucid-Icons-104175952") I can package up mine if you want. The background on the dock and indicators are also custom creations. Hit me up if you want those.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-12-28
Okay... the Victorian theme I was working on was seriously starting to depress me, so I put it on the back burner for now to work on a new theme.

Basically, I took the Dust Burnt theme, removed all the pixmaps and implanted all the Murrine settings from the Victorian theme.  Then I changed the color scheme to create a warm, sandy appearance.

GTK: Custom
Emerald: Custom
Wallpaper:  Excellium
Conky: Mira (heavily modified)
Dock: Cairo Dock with custom launchers
Font: Calibri
Icons: Eikon

Firefox theme:  Elementary.

I removed the folder icons and drop down arrows from the Bookmarks toolbar, reduced the height of the addressbar, and installed a Stylish theme that makes the tabs appear as buttons.  The Google theme is "Dark Gray Google" with a custom color modification.

[[IMG]http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/th_Screenshot-2-1.png[/IMG]](http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/Screenshot-2-1.png) [[IMG]http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/th_Screenshot-1-1.png[/IMG]](http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/Screenshot-1-1.png) [[IMG]http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/th_Screenshot-4.png[/IMG]](http://i279.photobucket.com/albums/kk122/SpecKtacle/Screenshot-4.png)

I apologize for the small size of the images.  I'm using my cell phone for internet and the upload speeds prevent me from uploading them here.  I had to upload them to Photobucket which reduces the size of the image.

### Post by Giant Speck on 2008-12-28
> **billgoldberg said:**
> Care to share you're conky?

I'm mostly intrested in the background of the conky file, or is that a wallpaper trick?

It's something to do with the conky config.  I'm just a beginner with conky, so all I really did was modify the Mira set.  Here is the config for the system conky (the centermost):

```
# Use Xft?
use_xft yes
xftfont cure:size=6

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
own_window  yes
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type widget
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 280 5

maximum_width 87

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders yes

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 0

# border margins
border_margin 5

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color 666252
#default_shade_color white
#default_outline_color black
own_window_colour 1B1A18

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 10
gap_y 318

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer yes

TEXT
${color D3CAAA}Kernel:${color a4a4a4}${alignr}$kernel
${color D3CAAA}UpTime:${color a4a4a4}${alignr}$uptime

${color D3CAAA}CPU 1:${color a4a4a4}${alignr}${cpu cpu1}% ${color D3CAAA}${execi 20 sensors k8temp-pci-00c3 |grep Core0 |awk '{print $3}'}
${color A39C83}${cpugraph cpu1 10,85 D3CAAA D3CAAA} 

${color D3CAAA}CPU 2:${color a4a4a4}${alignr}${cpu cpu2}% ${color D3CAAA}${execi 20 sensors k8temp-pci-00c3 |grep Core1 |awk '{print $3}'}
${color A39C83}${cpugraph cpu2 10,85 D3CAAA D3CAAA} 

${color D3CAAA}RAM:${color a4a4a4}${alignr}$mem
${color A39C83}${membar 3,85}
```

---

### Post by N00b-un-2 on 2008-12-28
Here is my desktop.

GTK/Metacity Theme; modified Slickness-Black theme. I inverted most of the colors so that text is easier to read, and I changed some of the graphics.  Check out the window buttons.  They're based on Shiki Color metacity theme.

Icons:  A VERY heavily modified icon set.  It started out as Black-white_2, but now it has elements from Linsta3.0, Crashbit, Black-white, and a handful of icons that I made myself (notice the Fruity Loops icon in the dock.  Originally designed to match the grey/black theme)  Maybe soon I will package my custom icon set and put it on gnome look.

Dock: Cairo Dock.  I was using AWN.  AWN seemed to be more solid and easy to configure but it was limited but I hate the fact that you can't have just launchers without tasks too.  That's what the TASK bar is for.  Linux isn't Mac and it should try to imitate either.  SO STOP WITH THE MAC4LIN CRAP!!!  If you like OSX, buy a Mac... or install a Hackintosh distro.

Check out my Conky!  I just got the "Now Playing" and "Weather" applets to work.  I was using Screenlets to monitor my system, but Conky uses a lot less system resources.  I've noticed a decrease in ram usage of an average of 10% most of the time, and my CPU usage has dropped as well.

### Post by Richard9795 on 2008-12-30
A Simple, Good Looking Desktop, Easy to The Eye. I will Post the Wallpaper if wanted.

### Post by eightmillion on 2008-12-30
> **open_coder said:**
> Which plasmoid is that? The one that displays the album art and lyrics information.

That's a karamba theme. You can get it [here.]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Amarok+2+Simple?content=93541") The lyrics are done with a python script and conky. You can get that [here.]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Lyricsdownloader+for+Conky?content=94262")

The widget style is Bespin.

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2008-12-30
> **Islington said:**
> whats the rssbar from?

edit: scratch that, gimme all the details plox.

DE is Xfce 4.6 beta (an old beta since no one updated the PPA).

gtk+ and emerald/xfwm4 themes are my *Night-owl* themes. Can upload upon request but otherwise CBFed.

Icons are Eikon2 - see What is in a name?'s sig.

Thing in the middle of the screen is the, "Live Previews", for the compiz Wall plugin (got tired of the cube).

RSS bar is, as stated previously, conky. Same as the version ddnev45 linked to, except I've gone back to grey for the borders and I've added *own_window_title conkyrss* so I can make it selectively transparent in compiz.

Edit: Oh and the wallpaper is from interfacelift.com. Just sort by most recent and it'll be right at the top of the list.

> **dannytatom said:**
> The RSS bar is [Snackr](http://snackr.net/), no clue about the rest.No, it's not Snackr but I believe Snackr was where I got the original idea from.
